6 min
Punishments for Highway Robbery and Conditions for Repentance
Details the hadd punishments based on Quran 5:33-34 and conditions for repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi interpretation of Quran 5:33-34 regarding the penalties for highway robbery, explain the distinction between tawzi' and takhyir for the word 'aw', and apply the condition that genuine repentance requires visible reform.

Core Idea
The four penalties in Quran 5:33 are distributed by crime type, not left to the ruler's choice.

This lesson examines the hadd punishments for hirabah (highway robbery) as derived from Quran 5:33-34. The central debate is whether the word 'aw' (or) grants the ruler discretion or distributes penalties based on the gravity of the offense. The Hanafi school adopts the latter, and also interprets 'nafy' (exile) as imprisonment to ensure deterrence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage concerns highway robbery (hirabah). The ruling is that penalties from the Quran apply depending on the nature of the crime.
Different scenarios trigger different penalties.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 5:33-34.
The verse lists four penalties connected by 'aw'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'aw' is interpreted as distributive (tawzi') based on early authorities like Ibn Abbas, not as choice (takhyir). Also, 'nafy' is interpreted as imprisonment rather than banishment.
The interpretation of 'aw' is crucial for determining the correct penalty.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Salaf held takhyir; some interpreted nafy as expulsion from Dar al-Islam.
These alternative views are considered less sound.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The correct view is tawzi' and imprisonment, as supported by the need for deterrence and narrated from Ibn Abbas.
Al-Fath (Ibn al-Humam) preferred this interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَأُخِذَ قبل أخذ شيءٍ وقتل حبس حتى يتوب وإن أخذ مالاً يصيب لكل واحد منه نصاب السرقة
(وإن أخذ مالاً
[2]قوله : حبس ؛ الأصل في هذا الباب قوله تعالى في سورة المائدة : ( إِنَّمَا جَزَاؤُا الَّذِينَ يُحَارِبُونَ اللهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَسْعَوْنَ فِي الْأَرْضِ فَسَادًا أَن يُقَتَلُوا أَوْ يُصَلَّبُوا أَوْ تُقَطَّعَ أَيْدِيهِمْ وَأَرْجُلُهُم مِّنْ خِلَافٍ أَوْ يُنفَوْا مِن الْأَرْضِ ذَلِكَ لَهُمْ خِزْيٌ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَلَهُمْ فِي الْآخِرَةِ عَذَابٌ عَظِيمُ إِلَّا الَّذِينَ تَابُوا مِن قَبْلِ أَن تَقْدِرُوا عَلَيْهِمْ فَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ ) (1). وكلمة «أو» في هذه الآية ظنّ بعض السلف أنها للتخيير، وأن الإمام مخير بين هذه الأجزية، فيقيم على القاطع ما شاء منها. والصحيح أن «أو» هاهنا للتوزيع على اختلاف الأحوال، وهو المنقول عن ابن عباس ، أخرجه الشافعي له في «الأم» ، وعبد الرزاق، وابن أبي شَيْبَة، وعبد ابن حميد، والبيهقي، وغيرهم. ثم المراد بالنفي عند بعض السلف الإخراج من دار الإسلام إلى دار الحرب، والصحيح أن المراد به الحبس، فإنّ النفي بمعنى الإخراج لا يفيد زجراً ولا دفع شرّ، فإنّه يقطع المارة في البلدة الأخرى، كذا في «الفتح» (3).
[3]قوله : أي يظهر ؛ أشار به إلى أنه لا تكفي مجرّد الاستغفار اللساني في التوبة لإخراجه من السجن، بل معتبر ظهور علامات الصلاح والتقوى عليه.
[4]قوله : يصيب ؛ الجملة صفة لمال، وأشار به إلى أنه لو أخذوا مالاً أصاب كلّ واحد منهم مقدار قليل لم يقطع واحد منهم.
Then if he is caught before taking anything and killing, he is imprisoned until he repents. And if he takes property, and it reaches each one of them the nisab of theft. (And if he takes property) [2] His statement: 'imprisoned'; the basis in this chapter is the statement of Allah, the Exalted, in Surah al-Ma'idah: 'Indeed, the penalty for those who wage war against Allah and His Messenger and strive upon earth [to cause] corruption is only that they be killed or crucified or that their hands and feet be cut off from opposite sides or that they be exiled from the land. That is for them a disgrace in this world; and for them in the Hereafter is a great punishment, except for those who return [repent] before you apprehend them. And know that Allah is Forgiving and Merciful.' (5:33-34) And the word 'or' (aw) in this verse, some of the Salaf thought it was for choice (takhyir), and that the Imam is given choice between these penalties, so he imposes on the highway robber whichever he wishes. But the correct view is that 'or' here is for distribution (tawzi') according to different circumstances, and this is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, as recorded by al-Shafi'i in al-Umm, 'Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shaybah, 'Abd ibn Humayd, al-Bayhaqi, and others. Then what is meant by 'exile' (nafy) according to some of the Salaf is expulsion from Dar al-Islam to Dar al-Harb, but the correct view is that it means imprisonment, because exile in the sense of expulsion does not serve as a deterrent nor prevention of evil, as he would simply cut off travelers in another town. Thus in 'al-Fath' (3). [3] His statement: 'i.e., appears' — he indicated by it that mere verbal asking for forgiveness is not sufficient for repentance to remove him from prison; rather, the appearance of signs of righteousness and piety upon him is considered. [4] His statement: 'it reaches' — the clause is a description of the property, and he indicated by it that if they take property and each one of them receives only a small amount, not one of them is subject to hadd.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that explains the penalties for highway robbery. It begins by stating the ruling: if the robber is caught before taking any property and before killing anyone, he is imprisoned until he repents. However, if he takes property, then the hadd of hand and foot amputation (from opposite sides) applies only if each robber receives a share equal to the nisab of theft (the minimum threshold for theft hadd). The commentator then provides the primary textual proof: Quran 5:33-34. The verse lists four penalties: execution, crucifixion, amputation of hands and feet from opposite sides, and exile (nafy). A key interpretative issue is the word 'aw (or). Some early scholars (Salaf) understood it as giving the Imam a free choice among these penalties. However, the correct Hanafi interpretation (ascribed to Ibn 'Abbas and supported by many narrations) is that 'or' here is distributive (li al-tawzi'), meaning each penalty corresponds to a specific type of crime. For example, if the robber only kills, execution; if he kills and takes property, crucifixion; if he only takes property, amputation; if he terrorizes but takes nothing, exile. This is the Hanafi position. The commentator further clarifies the meaning of 'nafy' (exile). Some understood it as banishment from the Islamic lands to non-Muslim lands. But the correct view is that it means imprisonment, because simply expelling the criminal would not prevent him from committing the same crime elsewhere. Imprisonment serves as a deterrent and protects society. The commentator then addresses repentance: for the punishment to be lifted, mere verbal repentance (istighfar) is not enough; the criminal must show visible signs of righteousness and piety (i.e., genuine reform). Finally, if a group takes property but the share per person is less than the nisab, the hadd of amputation does not apply to any of them.

Key Terms
نفي (nafy): Exile or banishment; in this context, the correct Hanafi interpretation is imprisonment.
توزيع (tawzi'): Distribution; the grammatical function of 'aw' indicating that each penalty applies to a specific circumstance, not a choice.
توبة (tawbah): Repentance that lifts the hadd penalty; requires genuine reform and visible signs of righteousness, not mere verbal confession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation of Quran 5:33, the word 'aw' (or) is understood as:
A) Takhyir (choice) – the Imam may choose any penalty.
B) Tawzi' (distribution) – each penalty is for a specific type of crime.
C) Takhsis (specification) – some penalties are abrogated.
D) Ta'mim (generalization) – all penalties apply to all cases.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of Quran 5:33 distributes penalties according to the crime, interprets 'nafy' as imprisonment, and requires genuine repentance for remission of punishment.

Imprisonment Until Repentance: Ruling for the Highway Robber Captured Before Theft
Ruling on detention until repentance for robber captured before taking property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a highway robber captured before taking property and identify the Quranic proof and its interpretation regarding imprisonment.

Core Idea
A highway robber captured before theft is imprisoned until genuine repentance is proven, based on Quran 5:33-34.

The law of highway robbery (hirabah) includes specific punishments tailored to the criminal's actions. One scenario is when the robber is captured before taking any property or killing. What punishment applies? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that such a robber is imprisoned until his repentance is evidenced by outward signs of righteousness. We will explore the Quranic basis and the interpretive choices that distinguish the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question: a highway robber (qati' al-tariq) is captured before taking any property or committing murder. According to the Hanafi school, the ruling is imprisonment (habs) until repentance (tawbah) is proven by outward signs of piety.
Repentance here is not merely verbal but must be demonstrated by a change in conduct.
2
Locate the dalil
The ruling is derived from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:33-34), which lists punishments for those who wage war against Allah and His Messenger. The Hanafi school interprets the word 'or' in the verse as indicating distribution (tawzi') based on the severity of the crime, not as a free choice for the Imam.
The verse mentions exile (nafy) which Hanafis interpret as imprisonment.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof for imprisonment: the verse includes 'exile from the land' (nafy). The Hanafi view equates this with imprisonment because banishment does not effectively deter or prevent further harm. The exception for repentance before capture confirms that repentance after capture does not stop the prescribed punishment, but does allow eventual release if genuine.
The condition that the victim must be a protected person (ma'sum) is also derived from the context of the verse.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early scholars (Salaf) understood 'or' in the verse as giving the Imam a choice (takhyir) between punishments. The Hanafi school, following Ibn Abbas and others, insists on distribution (tawzi') – each punishment corresponds to a specific criminal act.
Also, some interpreted exile literally as banishment, but Hanafis reject that as ineffective.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the stronger one because it is based on the purpose of the punishment (deterrence) and the report from Ibn Abbas. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view is imprisonment until repentance.
The authority is Zahir al-Riwayah, and the ruling is wajib as it is a hadd punishment.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran. It addresses a highway robber (qati' al-tariq) who is captured before taking any property. The ruling is that he is imprisoned until he repents, with repentance being evidenced by outward signs of righteousness, not mere words. The proof is verse 5:33-34 which lists punishments for muharibun. The commentator clarifies that 'or' in the verse indicates distribution of punishments based on the criminal's actions, not a free choice for the Imam. The Hanafi interpretation is that 'exile' in the verse refers to imprisonment, not banishment. Additionally, the ruling only applies if the victim is a protected person (Muslim or dhimmi); if the victim is a musta'min (temporary safe-conduct), the punishment is ta'zir, not hadd. Finally, if multiple robbers take property, the hadd of cutting is only applied if each individually acquires the nisab of theft.

Key Terms
معصوم (ma'sum): A person whose life and property are inviolable in Islamic law, specifically a Muslim or a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim).
حبس (habs): Imprisonment as a punitive measure, equated with 'exile' (nifay) in the Quranic verse, meaning confinement rather than banishment.
توبة (tawbah): Repentance that must be evidenced by outward signs of righteousness and piety, not merely verbal confession.
نصاب السرقة (nisab al-sariqah): The minimum value of stolen property required for the application of the hadd of amputation, which must be individually met by each robber.

Hadd Punishments for Highway Robbery: Three Scenarios
Rulings on varied punishments for highway robbery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of highway robbery (property only, killing only, both) and apply the correct hadd punishment for each, explaining why the execution for killing alone is not pardonable by the victim's heir.

Core Idea
Highway robbery punishments are fixed by Allah; the Imam's discretion only arises when both killing and theft occur.

The Qur'anic verse 5:33 prescribes punishments for those who wage war against Allah and His Messenger. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the Hanafi application: each distinct act (taking property without killing, killing without taking property, and both together) triggers a specific hadd penalty. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three criminal acts
From the passage, identify the three scenarios: (1) taking property without killing, (2) killing without taking property, (3) killing and taking property together.
2
State the hadd punishment for each scenario
For (1): amputation of right hand and left foot. For (2): execution as a hadd penalty, not qisas – so the victim's heir cannot pardon. For (3): the Imam has discretion among several options: amputation then execution, amputation then crucifixion, amputation with execution and crucifixion, execution alone, or crucifixion alone.
The amputation is conditional on sound limbs; if a limb is missing or paralyzed, the punishment is adjusted.
3
Explain why killing without theft is hadd not qisas
Because the robber's act is considered a violation of public order (hirabah), not merely a private killing. Hence it is a fixed penalty (hadd) that cannot be waived by the victim's family.
This distinguishes it from murder subject to qisas, where the heir may pardon or demand blood money.
4
Describe the conditions for amputation
The passage states that amputation is from opposite sides (right hand, left foot) and only if both limbs are sound. If the left hand is paralyzed, the right hand is not cut; if the right hand is already cut, the left hand is not cut; similar for the foot.
These conditions ensure the punishment is applied as prescribed and does not exceed its intended severity.
5
Detail the Imam's discretion when both killing and theft occur
The Imam may choose among the listed options. The passage also describes the method of crucifixion: a wooden structure is erected, and the robber is fixed to it. If crucifixion alone is chosen, he is crucified alive and his belly is slit; if combined with execution, killing precedes crucifixion.
This discretion allows the Imam to tailor the punishment to the severity of the crime.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[١] قوله : من خلاف ؛ - بكسر الخاء - ؛ أي من الجانبين، فتقطع اليد اليمنى والرجل اليسرى، وهذا إذا كان صحيح الأطراف، فلو كانت يُسراه شلاء لم تقطع يمينه وكذا لو كانت ( رجله اليسرى، ولو كان مقطوع اليمنى لم تقطع يده، وكذا الرجل اليسرى، كذا في «النهر). [٢]قوله : وإن قتل ؛ أي إن قتل القاطع معصوماً بدون أخذ شيء من الأموال قتل، وهذا القتل حدّ للقاطع لا قصاص، فلو عفا عنه ولي لا يعتبر به. [٣] قوله : حداً ؛ ولهذا لا يشترط أن يكون قتله موجباً للقصاص، فيقتل القاتل والمعين سواء قتل بسيف أو بحجر أو عصا على ما سيأتي في المتن. [٤] قوله : فلا يعفوه ولي ؛ لكونه حداً خالصاً الله لا يسع فيه عفو غيره ، فمن عفا عنه فقد عصى الله ورسوله، كذا في «الفتح». [0]قوله : قطع ... الخ ؛ الحاصل إنّ في صورة صدور قتل وأخذ مال منه الإمام مخير بين أمور، فإن شاء قطعه من خلاف ثمّ قتل، وإن شاءَ صلبه بعد القطع من خلاف، وإن شاء جمع بين القطع والصلب والقتل، وإن شاءَ قتل فقط، وإن شاء صلب فقط. (٦) قوله : أو صلب ؛ بأن تغرز خشبة في الأرض ثم يربط عليها خشبة أخرى عرضاً، فيضع قدمه عليها، ويربط من أعلا خشبة أخرى ويربط عليها يداه ، كذا في «الجوهرة» (۳). His hand and foot are cut from opposite sides. If he kills without taking [property], he is killed as a hadd penalty, not as qisas, so the heir cannot pardon him. If he kills and takes property, he is cut then killed or crucified, or killed, or crucified alive. [Commentary: [1] His statement: 'from opposite sides' – with a kasrah on the kha' – meaning from both sides, so the right hand and left foot are cut. This applies if his limbs are sound. If his left hand is paralyzed, his right hand is not cut; similarly if his left foot is [paralyzed]; and if his right hand is already cut, his hand [the left?] is not cut, and similarly the left foot, as in al-Nahr. [2] His statement: 'If he kills' – meaning if the highway robber kills a protected person without taking any property, he is killed. This killing is a hadd for the robber, not qisas, so if the heir pardons him, it is not considered. [3] His statement: 'as a hadd' – therefore it is not required that his killing be subject to qisas; the killer and the one who assists are killed whether they killed with a sword, a stone, or a stick, as will come in the text. [4] His statement: 'the heir cannot pardon him' – because it is a pure hadd for Allah, in which pardon by others is not permitted; whoever pardons him has disobeyed Allah and His Messenger, as in al-Fath. [0] His statement: 'cut... etc.' – the summary: in the case of both killing and taking property, the Imam has discretion among several matters: if he wishes, he cuts him from opposite sides then kills him; if he wishes, he crucifies him after cutting from opposite sides; if he wishes, he combines cutting, crucifixion, and killing; if he wishes, he kills only; if he wishes, he crucifies only. (6) His statement: 'or crucified' – by planting a wooden post in the ground, then tying another wooden beam across it, placing his feet on it, and tying another beam above and tying his hands to it, as in al-Jawharah. [7] His statement: 'alive' – this applies if the Imam chooses crucifixion only; then he crucifies him alive and slits his belly. If he chooses to combine killing and crucifixion, then killing precedes.]
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage details the punishments for highway robbery based on the criminal's actions. It is based on the Qur'anic verse (5:33) which lists four punishments: execution, crucifixion, amputation of opposite limbs, and exile. The commentator explains each scenario: (1) If the robber takes property but does not kill, the punishment is amputation of the right hand and left foot from opposite sides, provided both limbs are sound; if a limb is missing or paralyzed, the amputation is adjusted as per the detailed rules. (2) If the robber kills without taking property, he is executed as a hadd punishment, not as qisas, meaning the victim's heir has no right to pardon or waive the execution. (3) If the robber both kills and takes property, the Imam has discretion among several punishments: amputation followed by execution, amputation followed by crucifixion, amputation with execution and crucifixion, execution alone, or crucifixion alone. The text also describes the method of crucifixion: the robber is fixed to a wooden structure. If crucifixion alone is chosen, the robber is crucified alive and his belly is slit; if combined with execution, killing precedes crucifixion.

Key Terms
من خلاف (min khilaf): From opposite sides: cutting the right hand and left foot.
صلب (salb): Crucifixion: fixing the criminal to a wooden structure as a punishment.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah, not subject to pardon or reduction by human authorities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the punishment for a highway robber who kills a protected person without taking any property?
A) Amputation of the right hand and left foot.
B) Execution as a hadd penalty, not pardonable by the victim's family.
C) Execution only if the victim's heir agrees.
D) Imprisonment until repentance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, highway robbery triggers fixed hadd penalties that vary based on the acts committed, and the Imam has discretion only when both killing and theft occur.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
The Specific Punishments for Highway Robbery in Hanafi Fiqh
States the four hadd punishments for different types of highway robbery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of highway robbery and identify the specific hadd punishment prescribed for each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Highway robbery punishment is tied precisely to the crime: cutting for theft, execution for killing, crucifixion for both, exile for terror.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on highway robbery (qat' al-tariq). The school holds that the punishments are fixed by divine law according to the type of offense committed. You will learn the conditions for each punishment and the rationale behind the choice the imam has in certain cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of highway robbery
The text mentions four scenarios: taking property only, killing only, killing and taking property, and mere terrorization.
These correspond to the four punishments in the verse.
2
Match each crime to its specific hadd punishment
For taking property only -> cutting right hand and left leg from opposite sides. For killing only -> execution as hadd (not qisas). For killing and taking -> imam chooses among several severe punishments. For terrorizing only -> exile.
3
Understand the conditions for cutting from opposite sides
The limb must be sound; if missing or paralyzed, the corresponding limb on the other side is not cut.
4
Recognize why the punishment is hadd not qisas
It is a right of Allah, so the victim's guardian cannot pardon it.
This distinguishes it from qisas where pardon is allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السرقة باب قطع الطريق
قطع يده ورجله من خلاف. وإن قتل بلا أخذ قُتِلَ حداً لا قصاصاً، فلا يعفوه ولي.
وإن قتل وأخذ مالاً قطع ثُمّ قتل أو صلب، أو قتل، أو صلب حياً
قُطِعَ يده ورجله من خلاف"
[١] وإن قتل بلا أخذ قُتِلَ حداً " لا قصاصاً ) : أي هذا القتل بطريق الحد لا بطريق القصاص، فذكر ثمرة هذا بقوله : ( فلا يعفوه ولي )
[0]
وإن قتل وأخذ مالا قطع ثم قتل أو صلب، أو قتل، أو صلب حيا) [١] قوله : من خلاف ; - بكسر الخاء - ; أي من الجانبين، فتقطع اليد اليمنى والرجل اليسرى، وهذا إذا كان صحيح الأطراف، فلو كانت يُسراه شلاء لم تقطع يمينه وكذا لو كانت ( رجله اليسرى، ولو كان مقطوع اليمنى لم تقطع يده، وكذا الرجل اليسرى، كذا في «النهر). [٢]قوله : وإن قتل ; أي إن قتل القاطع معصوماً بدون أخذ شيء من الأموال قتل، وهذا القتل حدّ للقاطع لا قصاص، فلو عفا عنه ولي لا يعتبر به. [٣] قوله : حداً ; ولهذا لا يشترط أن يكون قتله موجباً للقصاص، فيقتل القاتل والمعين سواء قتل بسيف أو بحجر أو عصا على ما سيأتي في المتن. [٤] قوله : فلا يعفوه ولي ; لكونه حداً خالصاً الله لا يسع فيه عفو غيره ، فمن عفا عنه فقد عصى الله ورسوله، كذا في «الفتح». [0]قوله : قطع ... الخ ; الحاصل إنّ في صورة صدور قتل وأخذ مال منه الإمام مخير بين أمور، فإن شاء قطعه من خلاف ثمّ قتل، وإن شاءَ صلبه بعد القطع من خلاف، وإن شاء جمع بين القطع والصلب والقتل، وإن شاءَ قتل فقط، وإن شاء صلب فقط. (٦) قوله : أو صلب ; بأن تغرز خشبة في الأرض ثم يربط عليها خشبة أخرى عرضاً، فيضع قدمه عليها، وربط من أعلا خشبة أخرى ويربط عليها يداه ، كذا في «الجوهرة» (۳). [٧]قوله : حيّاً ; هذا إذا اختار الإمام صلبه فقط ، فيصلبه حياً ويشق بطنه، وإن اختار الجمع بين القتل والصلب، فالقتل يكون سابقاً.
(۱) «النهر الفائق»(۳: ۱۹۱).
(۲) «فتح القدير (٥ : ٤٢٤). (۳) «الجوهرة النيرة» (۲ : ۱۷۳).

فقوله : أو قتل ، عطف على قطع : أي إن شاء قطع ثُمَّ قتل أو صلب، وإن شاءَ
(1)
قُتِلَ أو صُلِبَ حيَّا من غير قطع " [١] قوله : أي إن شاء ; قال في «نور الأنوار»: إنّ الله قد نقل للمحاربين ولساعي الفساد ; أعني قطاع الطريق أربعة أجزية من القطع، والصلب، وقطع الأيدي والأرجل من خلاف، والنفي بطريق الترديد بكلمة «أو».
فمالك الله يقول : إنّها على حالها، فيتخير الإمام بينها.
وعندنا بمعنى «بل» للإضراب ; لأنّ جنايات قطاع الطريق كانت على أربعة أنواع : أعني أخذ المال فقط، والقتل فقط، والقتل وأخذ المال جميعاً، والتخويف فقط من غير قتل وأخذ ، فقابل بهذه الجنايات الأربع الأجزية الأربعة، ولكن لم يذكر الجنايات في النص اعتماداً على فهم العاقلين، وذلك لأنّ الجزاء إنما يكون على حسب الجناية، فغلظها بغلظه وخفتها بخفته، ولا يليقُ من الحكيم المطلق أن يقابل أغلظ الجناية بأخفها أو بالعكس. فكان تقدير عبارة القرآن أن يقتلوا إذا قتلوا فقط، ويصلبوا إذا ارتفعت المحاربة بقتل النفس وأخذ المال بل تقطع أيديهم وأرجلهم إذا أخذوا المال فقط ، بل ينفوا من الأرض إذا خوّفوا الطريق.
وقد وَرَدَ هذا البيان بعينه عن النبي له أنه أودع أبا بردة على أن لا يعينه ولا يعين عليه، فجاء أناس يريدون الإسلام، فقطع أصحاب أبي بردة عليهم الطريق، فنزل جبريل بالحد فيهم : إنّ من قتل وأخذ المال صلب، ومن قتل ولم يأخذ قتل، ومن أخذ المال ولم يقتل قطعت يده ورجله من خلاف ، ومن أفرد الإخافة نفي من الأرض.
(1) أي خير الإمام بين ست حالات إن شاء :
الأولى : القطع من خلاف ثم القتل.
الثانية : القطع ثم الصلب حيا. الثالثة : القطع ثم القتل ثم الصلب.
الرابع : القتل ثم الصلب.
الخامسة : القتل فقط.
السادسة : الصلب فقط حياً. ينظر : «الدر المختار»(۳: ۲۱۳).
Book of Theft, Chapter of Highway Robbery. He cuts his hand and leg from opposite sides. And if he kills without taking (property), he is killed as a hadd penalty, not as qisas, so the guardian may not pardon him. And if he kills and takes property, he is cut, then killed or crucified, or killed, or crucified alive. His hand and leg are cut from opposite sides. [1] 'And if he kills without taking, he is killed as a hadd penalty, not as qisas' means this killing is by way of hadd, not by way of qisas, so the fruit of this is mentioned in his statement: 'so the guardian may not pardon him'. [2] 'And if he kills and takes property, he is cut, then killed or crucified, or killed, or crucified alive'... His statement: 'from opposite sides' - with kasra on the kha - meaning from both sides, so the right hand and left leg are cut. This is if he is sound of limbs. If his left hand is paralyzed, his right hand is not cut, and similarly for his left leg. If his right hand is already cut, his hand is not cut, and similarly for the left leg. As in 'al-Nahr'. [2] His statement: 'And if he kills' means if the highway robber kills a protected person without taking anything, he is killed. This killing is a hadd for the robber, not qisas. So if the guardian pardons him, it is not considered. [3] His statement: 'as a hadd' - therefore it is not required that his killing be subject to qisas; the killer and the helper are both killed whether he kills with a sword, stone, or stick, as will come in the text. [4] His statement: 'so the guardian may not pardon him' because it is a pure hadd of Allah, in which there is no room for pardon by others. So whoever pardons him has disobeyed Allah and His Messenger, as in 'al-Fath'. [5] The conclusion: In the case where killing and taking property occur together, the imam has a choice between matters: if he wishes, he cuts from opposite sides then kills; if he wishes, he crucifies after cutting; if he wishes, he combines cutting, crucifixion, and killing; if he wishes, he kills only; if he wishes, he crucifies only. (6) His statement: 'or crucified' means a wooden pole is fixed in the ground, then another wooden pole is tied across it horizontally so that his foot is placed on it, and another pole is tied above and his hands are tied to it, as in 'al-Jawhara' (3). [7] His statement: 'alive' - this is if the imam chooses only crucifixion, so he crucifies him alive and splits his belly; but if he chooses to combine killing and crucifixion, killing precedes. (1) 'al-Nahr al-Faiq' (3:191), (2) 'Fath al-Qadir' (5:424), (3) 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' (2:173). Then his statement: 'or killed' is conjuncted to 'cut', meaning if he wishes, he cuts then kills or crucifies; but if he wishes, he is killed or crucified alive without cutting. [1] His statement: 'if he wishes' - in 'Nur al-Anwar': Allah has transferred for the muharibun (those who wage war) and spreaders of corruption - meaning highway robbers - four punishments: cutting, crucifixion, cutting hands and legs from opposite sides, and exile, by way of alternation with the word 'aw' (or). So Malik (Allah have mercy on him) says they are on the same level, thus the imam may choose between them. And in our school it means 'bal' (rather) for switching, because the crimes of highway robbers were of four types: taking property only, killing only, killing and taking property together, and just frightening without killing or taking. So these four crimes were matched with these four punishments. But the crimes are not mentioned in the text, relying on the understanding of intelligent people, because the recompense is according to the crime; its severity matches severity, and its lightness matches lightness. It is not befitting the absolutely Wise to match the worst crime with the lightest punishment or vice versa. So the estimation of the wording of the Quran is: they should be killed if they only kill; they should be crucified if waging war by killing and taking property; rather, their hands and legs should be cut if they only take property; rather, they should be exiled if they only terrorize the road. And this same explanation has been transmitted from the Prophet (PBUH) that he entrusted Abu Burda to not help him nor help against him, and some people came wanting to embrace Islam, but the companions of Abu Burda waylaid them. Then Jibril came down with the hadd concerning them: 'Whoever kills and takes property is crucified; whoever kills and does not take is killed; whoever takes property and does not kill, his hand and leg are cut from opposite sides; and whoever only terrorizes is exiled from the land.' (1) That is, the imam may choose among six cases if he wishes: First: cutting from opposite sides then killing. Second: cutting then crucifixion alive. Third: cutting then killing then crucifixion. Fourth: killing then crucifixion. Fifth: killing only. Sixth: crucifixion only alive. See 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' (3:213).
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) in the Hanafi school presents the rulings for various categories of highway robbers (muharibin). The base text (matn) first states the general punishment for robbery without killing: cutting the right hand and left leg from opposite sides. Then it distinguishes two scenarios: (1) if the robber kills but does not take property, he is executed as a fixed punishment (hadd), not as qisas (retaliation) — meaning the victim's guardian cannot pardon it; (2) if he both kills and takes property, the imam has a choice among several severe punishments: cutting from opposite sides followed by execution, crucifixion, or both. The commentary elaborates on the meaning of 'from opposite sides' (min khilaf), specifying that the right hand and left leg are cut, provided the limbs are sound. If a limb is already missing or paralyzed, the corresponding limb on the other side is not cut. The commentary also clarifies that the imam has six possible options when the robber kills and takes property, as listed at the end. A significant portion of the passage addresses the interpretation of Quran 5:33, where the word 'aw' (or) appears. According to the Hanafi school, this 'aw' means 'bal' (rather), indicating a differentiation based on the type of crime — not giving the imam free choice among punishments for any crime. Rather, each specific crime has its specific punishment. The commentary reports that Imam Malik held the opposite view (free choice), but the Hanafi position is supported by a hadith transmitted via Abu Burda, in which Jibril explicitly assigned punishments according to the nature of the offense.

Key Terms
قطع من خلاف (qat' min khilaf): Cutting the right hand and left leg from opposite sides; a specific punishment for highway robbery when only property is taken.
حداً (haddan): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah, not subject to pardon or commutation.
محارب (muharib): One who wages war (hirabah) by highway robbery, including killing, taking property, or terrorizing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a highway robber who only steals property is punished by:
A) Execution
B) Cutting from opposite sides
C) Crucifixion
D) Exile

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the punishment for highway robbery is strictly matched to the specific crime committed: cutting for theft, execution for killing, and a choice of severe penalties when both occur, with no pardon possible.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
advanced

The Hanafi Interpretation of Quran 5:33: Specific Punishments vs. Free Choice
Analyzes the Hanafi vs Maliki interpretation of the word 'aw' in Quran 5:33.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school interprets the word 'aw' in Quran 5:33 as 'bal' (rather) and how this leads to specific punishments, and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
The word 'aw' in the highway robbery verse means 'rather' for differentiation, not 'or' for choice, according to Hanafi usul.

This lesson delves into the interpretive dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding Quran 5:33. The key is the word 'aw' and whether it gives the imam free choice or requires matching punishment to crime. You will examine the Hanafi proof, including the hadith of Abu Burda, and understand the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verse in question
Quran 5:33 lists four punishments: execution, crucifixion, cutting from opposite sides, exile, connected by 'aw'.
The verse is the primary dalil.
2
Understand the Maliki reading
Imam Malik reads 'aw' as giving the imam free choice among the four punishments for any highway robbery.
This is based on the literal meaning.
3
Understand the Hanafi reading
The Hanafi school reads 'aw' as 'bal' (rather), meaning each punishment is assigned to a specific crime.
They argue this is more consistent with divine wisdom.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
The hadith of Abu Burda from the Prophet shows that Jibril differentiated the punishments according to the crime.
This is a specification (takhsis) of the general wording.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Hanafi, a robber who only kills gets execution only; under Maliki, the imam could choose a harsher punishment like crucifixion.
This affects the actual implementation.

[2] His statement: 'And if he kills' means if the highway robber kills a protected person without taking anything, he is killed. This killing is a hadd for the robber, not qisas. So if the guardian pardons him, it is not considered. [3] His statement: 'as a hadd' - therefore it is not required that his killing be subject to qisas; the killer and the helper are both killed whether he kills with a sword, stone, or stick, as will come in the text. [4] His statement: 'so the guardian may not pardon him' because it is a pure hadd of Allah, in which there is no room for pardon by others. So whoever pardons him has disobeyed Allah and His Messenger, as in 'al-Fath'. [5] The conclusion: In the case where killing and taking property occur together, the imam has a choice between matters: if he wishes, he cuts from opposite sides then kills; if he wishes, he crucifies after cutting; if he wishes, he combines cutting, crucifixion, and killing; if he wishes, he kills only; if he wishes, he crucifies only. (6) His statement: 'or crucified' means a wooden pole is fixed in the ground, then another wooden pole is tied across it horizontally so that his foot is placed on it, and another pole is tied above and his hands are tied to it, as in 'al-Jawhara' (3). [7] His statement: 'alive' - this is if the imam chooses only crucifixion, so he crucifies him alive and splits his belly; but if he chooses to combine killing and crucifixion, killing precedes. (1) 'al-Nahr al-Faiq' (3:191), (2) 'Fath al-Qadir' (5:424), (3) 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira' (2:173). Then his statement: 'or killed' is conjuncted to 'cut', meaning if he wishes, he cuts then kills or crucifies; but if he wishes, he is killed or crucified alive without cutting. [1] His statement: 'if he wishes' - in 'Nur al-Anwar': Allah has transferred for the muharibun (those who wage war) and spreaders of corruption - meaning highway robbers - four punishments: cutting, crucifixion, cutting hands and legs from opposite sides, and exile, by way of alternation with the word 'aw' (or). So Malik (Allah have mercy on him) says they are on the same level, thus the imam may choose between them. And in our school it means 'bal' (rather) for switching, because the crimes of highway robbers were of four types: taking property only, killing only, killing and taking property together, and just frightening without killing or taking. So these four crimes were matched with these four punishments. But the crimes are not mentioned in the text, relying on the understanding of intelligent people, because the recompense is according to the crime; its severity matches severity, and its lightness matches lightness. It is not befitting the absolutely Wise to match the worst crime with the lightest punishment or vice versa. So the estimation of the wording of the Quran is: they should be killed if they only kill; they should be crucified if waging war by killing and taking property; rather, their hands and legs should be cut if they only take property; rather, they should be exiled if they only terrorize the road. And this same explanation has been transmitted from the Prophet (PBUH) that he entrusted Abu Burda to not help him nor help against him, and some people came wanting to embrace Islam, but the companions of Abu Burda waylaid them. Then Jibril came down with the hadd concerning them: 'Whoever kills and takes property is crucified; whoever kills and does not take is killed; whoever takes property and does not kill, his hand and leg are cut from opposite sides; and whoever only terrorizes is exiled from the land.' (1) That is, the imam may choose among six cases if he wishes: First: cutting from opposite sides then killing. Second: cutting then crucifixion alive. Third: cutting then killing then crucifixion. Fourth: killing then crucifixion. Fifth: killing only. Sixth: crucifixion only alive. See 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' (3:213).
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on highway robbery (qat' al-tariq) in the Hanafi school presents the rulings for various categories of highway robbers (muharibin). The base text (matn) first states the general punishment for robbery without killing: cutting the right hand and left leg from opposite sides. Then it distinguishes two scenarios: (1) if the robber kills but does not take property, he is executed as a fixed punishment (hadd), not as qisas (retaliation) — meaning the victim's guardian cannot pardon it; (2) if he both kills and takes property, the imam has a choice among several severe punishments: cutting from opposite sides followed by execution, crucifixion, or both. The commentary elaborates on the meaning of 'from opposite sides' (min khilaf), specifying that the right hand and left leg are cut, provided the limbs are sound. If a limb is already missing or paralyzed, the corresponding limb on the other side is not cut. The commentary also clarifies that the imam has six possible options when the robber kills and takes property, as listed at the end. A significant portion of the passage addresses the interpretation of Quran 5:33, where the word 'aw' (or) appears. According to the Hanafi school, this 'aw' means 'bal' (rather), indicating a differentiation based on the type of crime — not giving the imam free choice among punishments for any crime. Rather, each specific crime has its specific punishment. The commentary reports that Imam Malik held the opposite view (free choice), but the Hanafi position is supported by a hadith transmitted via Abu Burda, in which Jibril explicitly assigned punishments according to the nature of the offense.

Key Terms
قطع من خلاف (qat' min khilaf): Cutting the right hand and left leg from opposite sides; a specific punishment for highway robbery when only property is taken.
حداً (haddan): A fixed punishment prescribed by Allah, not subject to pardon or commutation.
محارب (muharib): One who wages war (hirabah) by highway robbery, including killing, taking property, or terrorizing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the word 'aw' in Quran 5:33 is interpreted as:
A) Giving the imam free choice
B) 'bal' (rather) specifying punishments
C) Meaning 'and'
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school interprets Quran 5:33 as assigning specific punishments to specific crimes, based on the hadith of Abu Burda and rational consistency, in opposition to the Maliki view of free choice.
